No.(1)waspresented toHon\342\200\231ble Chairman, Rajya Sabhaonthe21stJanuary,2010,underDirection31(1) ofthe Directionsby the Chairman, Rajya Sabha.A copyofthe Report wasforwarded tothe Hon\342\200\231ble Speaker, Lok Sabha.", "03.03.20101712.03 \302\275 hrs.STATEMENT BY MINISTERStatus of implementation of therecommendations contained in the 23rdreportof Standing Committee on Personnel,Public Grievances, Lawand Justice onGovernment\342\200\231s policy for appointment on Compassionate grounds, pertainingto the Ministry of Personnel,Public Grievances and Pensions.\342\210\227THE MINISTER OFSTATE OFTHE MINISTRY OF SCIENCE ANDTECHNOLOGY; MINISTER OF STATE OF THE MINISTRY OF EARTHSCIENCES;  MINISTER OFSTATE INTHE PRIME MINISTER\342\200\231SOFFICE;MINISTER OF STATE INTHE MINISTRY OF PERSONNEL, PUBLICGRIEVANCES AND PENSIONS; AND MINISTER OF STATE IN THEMINISTRY OF PARLIAMENTARY AFFAIRS (SHRI PRITHVIRAJ CHAVAN):I beg to lay the statement.  The Department-Related Parliamentary StandingCommittee on Personnel, Public Grievances, Law & Justice had made 12recommendations in its 23rdReport on the Government\342\200\231s policy of Appointmenton Compassionate Ground. These recommendations were duly considered by theMinistry ofPersonnel,Public Grievancesand Pensionsandit was observed thateffective implementation of / action on these recommendations requiredconsultations with someotherMinistries / Departments. The matter wasaccordingly taken up with the Ministries/ Departments concerned. Comments /inputs were received fromthem. Having examined the matter in consultation witha number of other Ministries / Departments,e.g. Department ofFinancial Services,Department of Public Enterprises, Ministryof Health and Family Welfare, etc., anAction Taken Note was prepared and sentto the Rajya Sabha Secretariat on7.12.2009. CHITTHAN (DINDIGUL):Climate model projections summarizedin the latest Intergovernmental Panel onClimate Change(IPCC) report indicatethat the global surface temperature will rise from 1.1 to 6.40C (2.0 to 11.50F)during the twenty-firstcentury. The uncertaintyin this estimate arises from the useof models with differing sensitivity to greenhouse gas concentrations and the useof differing estimates of future greenhouse gas emissions. Someotheruncertainties include how warming and related changeswill vary from region toregion around the globe. Mostof the studies focus on the period up to the year2100. However, warming is expected tocontinue beyond the year2100 evenifemissions stop, because of the large heatcapacity of the Oceans and the longlifetime of Carbon dioxide in the atmosphere.Increasing global temperature will cause sea levels to rise and will changethe amountand pattern of precipitation, including expansion of subtropical deserts.The continuing retreat of glaciers, permafrost and sea ice is expected, with theArctic region being particularly affected. Other likely effects include shrinkage ofthe Amazon rainforest and Boreal forests,increase in the intensity of extremeweather events, species extinctions,and changes in agricultural yields.Human activity since the Industrial Revolution has increased the amountofgreenhouse gases in the atmospheres,leading to increased emission of CO2Methane,  CFCs and Nitrous Oxide.FurtherCO2concentrations are also continuing torise due to burning offossil fuels and land-usechange. Accordingly, theIPCCSpecial Report onEmissions Scenarios gives a widerange of future CO2scenarios, ranging from541to 970 ppmby the year 2100.  Fossil fuelreserves are sufficient to reach theselevels and continue emissionspast 2100 ifcoal, tar sands or Methane Clathratesare extensively exploited.", "03.03.201025I request the Central Government totake effective steps to mitigate theimpact of global warming.(vi) Need for re-alignment of bypass road connecting NH-5 to NH-9 viaVijayawada city in Andhra PradeshSHRI RAYAPATI SAMBASIVA RAO (GUNTUR):I would like to bring to thenotice of the Hon\342\200\231bleMinister of RoadTransport and Highways that NationalHighway Authority of India has proposedto develop a Bypass road to connect theNH-5 fromKanakadurgammaVaradhi near Soumya Apollo Hospital at 431/5 Km.up to NH-5 at Nidmanuru Village at14/5 km. \303\211\303\212B\303\211E\302\252\303\211\303\211 V\303\211\303\211A*SHRI ANTO ANTONY (PATHANAMATHITTA): Respected Madam, I take thisopportunity to inviteyour kind attention towards a serious matter.The existing interest subvention system forthe repayment of agriculturalloans in the countryadversely affects thefarmers in Kerala. It may be noted thatthe existing system was introducedthree years back. The new interest subventionsystemis based on Khariff and Rabiseasons. The Rabiseason starts on 1stOctoberand ends on 31stMarch. Agricultural loans for the Khariff crops are being releasedin the sameperiod. Khariff season starts on 1stApril and ends on 30thSeptember.In order to get the interest subvention for agricultural loans,the farmers have torepay the amounton or before 1stJune. This is also asymmetrical because the Rabicrops get a tenure of six months for repayment of agricultural loans and theKhariff crops get a tenure of three monthsfor the repaymentof the same.Thisinterest subvention system may be viable to the short-termcrops which fall underthe Khariff and Rabi seasons. But it is notfeasible for the farmers in Kerala,because the major cultivations in Kerala such ascoconut, rubber, banana, pepper,cardamometc. are long-termcrops and donot fall under Khariff and Rabi seasons.These crops need a long period for getting yield. Hence, the farmers in Kerala arenot able to repay the loan amount in the stipulated date and most of themhave toremit the full interest. It is a pity to negate themthe benefit of interest subventionin terms of Khariff and Rabiseasons in this hard time.Therefore, I request the Governmentto repeal the present systemand re-introduce the system thatwe had three years before. The systemexisted beforethree years had given aperiod of one yearfor the repayment of loans.As far as thefarmers in Kerala are concerned, this is the only viablesystem in which they getthe full benefits of interest subvention.", "03.03.2010114g\303\211\303\211\303\222 V\303\211M\303\211n\303\211\303\216\303\240\302\244\303\211B\303\211E\303\211{\303\211\303\211\303\243\303\211 LINGAM (TENKASI):MadamChairperson, I thank you for giving methis opportunityto raise an urgent matter of public importance while drawing thenotice of the Government, through this august House,about theplight of tribalpeople in the remote villages of my constituency and alsoof the poor agriculturallabourers who are losing their livelihood because of their being denied theirtraditional rights to graze the cattle inthe foothills of Western Ghats in myTenkasi constituency.In our country, traditional cattle grazing rights have provided livelihood tothe rural poor while contributing to the expansion of biodiversity. This also givesrise to increasing soil fertility due to the natural manure provided by the cattle tothe land in return for the grazing facility it gets. All these years, traditional cattlegrazing rights were available to the poorpeople living in the foothills of WesternGhats to take their cattle upto a height of 300 metres.Theynot only graze on thegrass but also provide natural manure tothe forest vegetation. In our country, foodproduction is reducing becauseof ourignoring the needs of poor farmersespecially in the foothill areas ofmountain ranges. Just because wildlifesanctuaries are announced without takinginto consideration the plight ofagricultural labour and landless farmers in the remotevillages, they are put togreat hardship. Theyhave to bear the bruntof forest officials too apart from theircrop loss caused by wild boars and other wild animals that get a free run becauseof those lands becoming inaccessible to farmers.* English translation ofthe speechoriginally delivered in Tamil.", "03.03.2010116In my constituency, particularly inVirudhunagar District forestland areas,in order to protect 400 grey squirrels, thatarea has been declared as a sanctuary.Similarly, in Tirunelveli District, takingthenameof tigers, forest land has beenmade inaccessible to the traditional cattlegrazers. This has resulted in non-availability of grass and fodder to the cattle causing depletion in cattle populationwhich affects agriculture and agriculturists. Farmers are prevented from staying intheir fields during the night and are not able to safeguard their agricultural producefrombeing destroyed by wild animals because of the free run they get in the wakeof that area being declared as wildlife sanctuary. In fact, cattle do not pose a threatto both forests andthe wild animals. Hence, I urgeupon the UnionGovernment tohave a re-look at the recent announcementsand restore the traditional rights of thepeople living there in the foothills ofWestern Ghats to carry on with theirtraditional cattle grazing occupation which will contribute to agriculturalproduction while allowing their livelihood to go on.SHRI K. SUGUMAR (POLLACHI): Madam Chairman, thank you for giving methis opportunityto raise an important issue regarding the plight of the coconutgrowers of Coimbatore, Tirupur and Erode districts of Tamil Nadu.The production cost of coconutis too high in comparison to the marketprice of the coconut.  The price of coconutis only 60 per cent compared to theyear 1990.  The cost of fertilizer, labour and other expenses havealso increasedcent per cent.  Due to the low costof coconut in the market, the growers are facinghuge problems.I had raised the samematter during the Question Hour of the Lok SabhavideQuestion No. 442.  While answering the Question, the hon. Minister told thatthe Government is paying Rs.44.50 asthe cost for one kilogramcopra andRs.12,000 per tonne for coconut.  In Tamil Nadu, coconuts are not procuredbutthe procurement of copra is going on.I had requested the hon. Minister, throughmy question, to start the procurement ofcoconuts for the welfare of the coconutgrowers.  While answering myquestion, thehon. Minister said that he would give", "03.03.2010117directions to the Government of Tamil Naduto start the procurement of coconuts.But till now, no action has been taken by the State Government as assured by thehon. Minister.While the procurement of coconut has already been started in the nearbyKerala State one month back, the adjacent districts like Coimbatore, Erode andTirupur in Tamil Nadu have beenneglected.  The Tamil Nadu Government is nottaking any action in this regard.  For the welfare of the coconut growers ofCoimbatore, Erode and Tirupur districts of Tamil Nadu,I would request thehon.Minister, through thisHouse, to directthe Tamil Nadu Government to start theprocurement of coconut inthe above said districts for the welfare of theagriculturists.
